<div id="review_241940134" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241940134" />
    <a title="Stepheny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny"><img alt="Stepheny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567725280p2/7091879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241940134?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stepheny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stepheny" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny">Stepheny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780670855032" href="/book/show/102417.Insomnia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=pantsless-platoon">pantsless-platoon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=all-hail-the-crimson-king">all-hail-the-crimson-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=reads-with-buddies">reads-with-buddies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=incredibly-sad-but-great">incredibly-sad-but-great</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=to-read-kindle">to-read-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=books-i-own-to-read">books-i-own-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=stephen-king-to-read">stephen-king-to-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241940134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14692088903415417491"><br/><br/>Since I’ve been on a bender writing reviews of books I didn’t enjoy, I think I’ll take a minute to write one about a book I enjoyed! <br/><br/>*think happy thoughts*<br/><br/>Insomnia was a buddy read with my <s>hostages</s> lttle band of misfits that are reading the Dark Tower together. I’ve read the DTS several times and knew that Insomnia had a few tie-ins with it, but this is the first time I had actually read it. I’m glad I did. The character that comes into play in the DTS is mentioned in this book but there’s not a</span>
  <span id="freeText14692088903415417491" style="display:none"><br /><br />Since I’ve been on a bender writing reviews of books I didn’t enjoy, I think I’ll take a minute to write one about a book I enjoyed! <br /><br />*think happy thoughts*<br /><br />Insomnia was a buddy read with my <s>hostages</s> lttle band of misfits that are reading the Dark Tower together. I’ve read the DTS several times and knew that Insomnia had a few tie-ins with it, but this is the first time I had actually read it. I’m glad I did. The character that comes into play in the DTS is mentioned in this book but there’s not a whole lot of development. Either way, I enjoyed Insomnia.<br /><br />Ralph can’t sleep. Duh! Did you read the name of this book?! He walks hoping to tire himself out enough to sleep at night, but as the days go by, he gets less and less sleep. While on one of these walks he witnesses his good friend who is normally a kind and personable man, flipping the fuuuuck out on another guy. He’s accusing this guy of killing children and even goes so far as to reach his hands into the vats of fertilizer he is transporting, believing that the man is hiding dead babies and children within those vats. Ralph is perplexed but believes it may have to do with the heat. Maybe his buddy is just having a rough day.<br /><br />Ralph’s wife dies and he continues to struggle sleeping. He begins to see things- auras. People have different colors around them and he thinks he is losing his mind. He soon finds out that he is not alone. You see, Lois- the GILF up the street- is also experiencing insomnia and seeing auras. Ralph and Lois swap stories and find out that they are a part of something big.<br /><br />The whole book centers around an upcoming event. The whole town is in an uproar. You see, this event, is a rally of sorts for a very big name in the pro-choice movement. Ralph’s buddy is leading the group of pro-lifers. But something isn’t quite right with him. He keeps talking about the Crimson King. Has he lost his mind? Is this about more than just abortion? <br /><br />Ralph and Lois soon find out that, whether they like it or not, they need to play a part in this upcoming event. And whether they like it or not, they’ll have some very hard decisions to make. <br /><br />The book was tedious at times, but I really loved Ralph. Lois I could have done without, but she didn’t annoy me enough to where she affected my enjoyment. Ralph is a diamond in the rough though. He is an instant favorite. ESPECIALLY after that ending!!! Talk about a hit in the feels! King doesn’t nail all of his endings, but this one was out of the park! <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14692088903415417491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau"><img alt="Ashley Daviau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599784716p2/35915119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1113634218?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Daviau" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau">Ashley Daviau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1113634218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7125257531767060778">This isn't my first time reading Insomnia, I think it may be my third or fourth time actually. But I definitely enjoyed it the most this time around! I gained a whole new love for this book on this read-through and I'm still stunned by all the Dark Tower references that I missed the other times I read this book! <br/><br/>I will admit that Insomnia is a bit slow at times and I did feel there was points were it dragged on a bit needlessly. But when it did pick up, it MORE than made up for the slow bits! Mo</span>
  <span id="freeText7125257531767060778" style="display:none">This isn't my first time reading Insomnia, I think it may be my third or fourth time actually. But I definitely enjoyed it the most this time around! I gained a whole new love for this book on this read-through and I'm still stunned by all the Dark Tower references that I missed the other times I read this book! <br /><br />I will admit that Insomnia is a bit slow at times and I did feel there was points were it dragged on a bit needlessly. But when it did pick up, it MORE than made up for the slow bits! More than once I kind of had to pause for a few minutes to absorb everything that was happening because it got pretty damn crazy at times! <br /><br />I really think this may be one of my top favourite King books, I just love everything about it so much! I find the whole concept of the story absolutely fascinating, I could get lost in thinking about it for days! And Ralph is such a gem of a character, I just love him to pieces! I mean all the characters are actually pretty great but he just holds a special place in my heart! <br /><br />I think my favourite part of this read-through though would have to be noticing all the Dark Tower references throughout. I had honestly never noticed them on my previous reads and seeing them all pop up this time around had me floored. It's actually quite mind blowing how intertwined this story is with the Dark Tower series! </span>

<div id="review_1660073862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1660073862" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1660073862?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451184962" href="/book/show/231603.Insomnia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1660073862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1729685880760354841"><i>Insomnia</i> in my opinion isn't as good as some of King's books, but it's still a really great story that joins into the frequent setting of the fictional small town of Derry, Maine, often present in King's works as the mysterious place where oddities and evil happens. In this particular one, it features an ordinary an whose lack of sleep allows him to see the monsters affecting everyone in town.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2323232294" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2323232294" />
    <a title="The Face of Your Father" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/79119566-the-face-of-your-father"><img alt="The Face of Your Father" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597595315p2/79119566.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2323232294?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Face of Your Father" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Face of Your Father" href="/user/show/79119566-the-face-of-your-father">The Face of Your Father</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2323232294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15233705343048312237">King's absolute best. Plus his most underappreciated. <br/><br/>“Sleep, that undiscriminating friend, humankind’s best and most reliable nurse since the dawn of time, has abandoned him again.”<br/><br/>One of my favorite lines from 'Insomnia'. What a great and desperate description of sleep. You can feel the exhaustion along with the frustration of Ralph Roberts because we've all been there with him. The line, while simple, is beautifully structured as if it is the closing line of some poetry. Above everything else</span>
  <span id="freeText15233705343048312237" style="display:none">King's absolute best. Plus his most underappreciated. <br /><br />“Sleep, that undiscriminating friend, humankind’s best and most reliable nurse since the dawn of time, has abandoned him again.”<br /><br />One of my favorite lines from 'Insomnia'. What a great and desperate description of sleep. You can feel the exhaustion along with the frustration of Ralph Roberts because we've all been there with him. The line, while simple, is beautifully structured as if it is the closing line of some poetry. Above everything else, King will always and truly be a poet deep down, his early love for poetry is relevant in all his works. <br /><br />'Insomnia' is my favorite novel of King's. This is King's imagination at its most wonderful wildest. There is the grief of losing a spouse, there is the topic of abortion, a sleeping disorder, auras glowing over people's heads, domestic violence, Dark Tower connections, terrorist plotting, Greek Mythology, this book is beautifully bonkers. <br /><br />The 90s were an interesting time for King's writings. This is the era of the strong women characters overcoming mistreatment, abuse &amp; injustices. From 'Dolores Claiborne' to 'Rose Madder' to 'Gerald's Game.' In 'Insomnia' a corrupted antagonist, Ed Deepneau savagely abuses his wife which comes to the attention of our protagonist, the elderly Ralph Roberts. Despite being much older than Ed, Ralph confronts him only to see Ed sitting on his front porch as he rants crazily about a Crimson King, thus setting the novel's events into motion. Ralph makes the choice to confront Ed about the domestic abuse which leads him down the path of saving what's most important, The Tower. A nice euphemism for the world. King is saying something powerful about domestic abuse, the fate of the universe relies on the reaction towards the domestic abuse. So many times it is ignored, so many times people are killed. This is King's boldest novel because he doesn't shy away from the uncomfortable topics, they are put directly into the reader's face because of the importance. Not only is ‘Insomnia’ the introduction to The Crimson King, it also contains King's most underappreciated villain, Atropos. A deliciously mischievous thing who keeps souvenirs from victims. This is the most important non-Dark Tower book in the DT series. The imagery is striking &amp; vivid, the themes are adult, the message is meaningful, the characters are inspiring, the stakes are high, the finale is lovely &amp; terrible. Mr. King, thankee-sai</span>
  <a data-text-id="15233705343048312237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

		    <b>
          <a title="Stephen King 2020 read-along" class="actionLink" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/19810028-may-read-yikes-already">Stephen King 2020...:</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('INeddnvZh/pXK2lrfyqP7nFgd81OIZqXm4HZp0R+1Aca8fSkwIdOkvAA3QqI34Uxpz+QBYCsFPDA/58WiT0mnQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Wtn7Y4yfAbCojw+vaQTXmUQF2Cu/upBIAQuDxo16dwpg/5KxN8HI2A+ku86e8d1Gklo/43E3Hi9adcV3QDmFkA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">Stephen King

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5843069205359225625">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText5843069205359225625" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5843069205359225625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
